      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Gold"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 112.00117924292px; border-left-color:Yellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 7.5541426254377px; border-left-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 1057.8894993406px 100px 0; border-right-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Benin (CIA World Factbook estimate 2013)<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (48.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (27.7%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Others / None (12.2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Gold; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Vodun" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodun">Vodun</a> (11.6%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg/220px-Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg/330px-Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg/440px-Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3135" data-file-height="1344"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Benin_-_batism_ceremony_in_Cotonou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Celestial_Church_of_Christ" title="Celestial Church of Christ">Celestial Church of Christ</a> baptism in Cotonou. Five percent of Benin's population belongs to this <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denomination</a>, an <a href="/wiki/African_Initiated_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="African Initiated Church">African Initiated Church</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Benin" title="Religion in Benin">Religion in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 2013 census, 48.5% of the population of Benin were <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (25.5% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, 6.7% <a href="/wiki/Celestial_Church_of_Christ" title="Celestial Church of Christ">Celestial Church of Christ</a>, 3.4% <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a>, 12.9% other Christian denominations), 27.7% were <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, 11.6% practiced <a href="/wiki/Vodun" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodun">Vodun</a>, 2.6% practiced other local traditional religions, 2.6% practiced other religions, and 5.8% claimed no religious affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-insae-bj.org_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insae-bj.org-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-report_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-53">[53]</a></sup> A government survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> Program in 2011-2012 indicated that followers of Christianity had increased to 57.5% of the population (with Catholics making up 33.9%, Methodists 3.0%, Celestials 6.2% and other Christians 14.5%), while Muslims had declined to 22.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2011-12_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2011-12-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditional religions include local <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animistic</a> religions in the <a href="/wiki/Atakora_Department" title="Atakora Department">Atakora</a> (Atakora and Donga provinces), and <a href="/wiki/Vodun" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodun">Vodun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orisha" title="Orisha">Orisha</a> veneration among the Yoruba and Tado peoples in the center and south of the nation. The town of <a href="/wiki/Ouidah" title="Ouidah">Ouidah</a> on the central coast is the spiritual center of Beninese Vodun. </p>
      <p>Today the two largest religions are Christianity, followed throughout the south and center of Benin and in <a href="/wiki/Otammari" class="mw-redirect" title="Otammari">Otammari</a> country in the <a href="/wiki/Atakora_Department" title="Atakora Department">Atakora</a>, and Islam, introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a> and Hausa merchants, and now followed throughout <a href="/wiki/Alibori" class="mw-redirect" title="Alibori">Alibori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borgou" class="mw-redirect" title="Borgou">Borgou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donga_Department" title="Donga Department">Donga</a> provinces, as well as among the Yoruba (who also follow Christianity). Many, however, continue to hold Vodun and Orisha beliefs and have incorporated the pantheon of Vodun and Orisha into Christianity. The <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslim_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmadiyya Muslim Community">Ahmadiyya Muslim Community</a>, a sect originating in the 19th century, is also present in a significant minority. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Benin" title="Geography of Benin">Geography of Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Benin_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Benin map of Köppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Benin, a narrow, north–south strip of land in West Africa, lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/Prime_meridian" title="Prime meridian">0°</a> and <a href="/wiki/4th_meridian_east" title="4th meridian east">4°E</a>. Benin is bounded by Togo to the west, <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Benin" title="Bight of Benin">Bight of Benin</a> to the south. The distance from the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a> in the north to the Atlantic Ocean in the south is about 650&nbsp;km (404&nbsp;mi). Although the coastline measures 121&nbsp;km (75&nbsp;mi), the country measures about 325&nbsp;km (202&nbsp;mi) at its widest point. Four terrestrial ecoregions lie within Benin's borders: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Guinean_forests" title="Eastern Guinean forests">Eastern Guinean forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_lowland_forests" title="Nigerian lowland forests">Nigerian lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-55">[55]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.86/10, ranking it 93rd globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg/220px-Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg/330px-Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg/440px-Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Atakora_Benin_Batia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Atakora_Department" title="Atakora Department">Atakora</a>, one of Benin's two northernmost departments.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:West_African_male_lion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/West_African_male_lion.jpg/220px-West_African_male_lion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/West_African_male_lion.jpg/330px-West_African_male_lion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/West_African_male_lion.jpg/440px-West_African_male_lion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1125" data-file-height="749"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:West_African_male_lion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Pendjari National Park in Benin is one of the most important reserves for the <a href="/wiki/West_African_lion" class="mw-redirect" title="West African lion">West African lion</a> and other large animals of West Africa.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Benin shows little variation in elevation and can be divided into four areas from the south to the north, starting with the low-lying, sandy, coastal plain (highest elevation 10&nbsp;m (32.8&nbsp;ft)) which is, at most, 10&nbsp;km (6.2&nbsp;mi) wide. It is marshy and dotted with lakes and lagoons communicating with the ocean. Behind the coast lies the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a>-covered plateaus of southern Benin (altitude between 20 and 200&nbsp;m (66 and 656&nbsp;ft)), which are split by valleys running north to south along the <a href="/wiki/Couffo_River" title="Couffo River">Couffo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zou_River" title="Zou River">Zou</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ou%C3%A9m%C3%A9_River" title="Ouémé River">Ouémé Rivers</a>. </p>
      <p>This geography makes it <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">vulnerable to climate change</a>. With the majority of the country living near the coast in low-lying areas sea level rise could have large effects on the economy and population.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Northern areas will see additional regions become deserts,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> making agriculture difficult in a region with many subsistence farmers. </p>
      <p>An area of flat land dotted with rocky hills whose altitude seldom reaches 400&nbsp;m (1,312&nbsp;ft) extends around Nikki and Save. </p>
      <p>A range of mountains extends along the northwest border and into Togo; these are the <a href="/wiki/Togo_Mountains" title="Togo Mountains">Atacora</a>. The highest point, <a href="/wiki/Mont_Sokbaro" title="Mont Sokbaro">Mont Sokbaro</a>, is at 658&nbsp;m (2,159&nbsp;ft). Benin has fallow fields, <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a>, and remnants of large sacred forests. In the rest of the country, the savanna is covered with thorny scrub and dotted with huge <a href="/wiki/Adansonia_digitata" title="Adansonia digitata">baobab</a> trees. Some forests line the banks of rivers. In the north and the northwest of Benin, the <a href="/wiki/W_National_Park" title="W National Park">Reserve du W du Niger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pendjari_National_Park" title="Pendjari National Park">Pendjari National Park</a> attract tourists eager to see elephants, lions, antelopes, hippos, and monkeys.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-49">[49]</a></sup> Pendjari National Park together with the bordering Parks <a href="/wiki/Arli_National_Park" title="Arli National Park">Arli</a> and <a href="/wiki/W_National_Park" title="W National Park">W</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> are among the most important strongholds for the endangered <a href="/wiki/West_African_lion" class="mw-redirect" title="West African lion">West African lion</a>. With an estimated 356 (range: 246–466) lions, W-Arli-Pendjari harbors the largest remaining population of lions in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Historically Benin has served as habitat for the endangered <a href="/wiki/Painted_hunting_dog" class="mw-redirect" title="Painted hunting dog">painted hunting dog</a>, <i>Lycaon pictus</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> however, this canid is thought to have been locally <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">extirpated</a>. </p>
      <p>Benin's climate is hot and humid. Annual rainfall in the coastal area averages 1300&nbsp;mm or about 51&nbsp;inches. Benin has two rainy and two dry seasons per year. The principal rainy season is from April to late July, with a shorter less intense rainy period from late September to November. The main dry season is from December to April, with a short cooler dry season from late July to early September. Temperatures and humidity are high along the tropical coast. In <a href="/wiki/Cotonou" title="Cotonou">Cotonou</a>, the average maximum temperature is 31&nbsp;°C (87.8&nbsp;°F); the minimum is 24&nbsp;°C (75.2&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-bn_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Variations in temperature increase when moving north through <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> and plateau toward the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>. A dry wind from the Sahara called the <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">Harmattan</a> blows from December to March, when grass dries up, other vegetation turns reddish brown, and a veil of fine dust hangs over the country, causing the skies to be overcast. It is also the season when farmers burn brush in the fields.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Benin" title="Economy of Benin">Economy of Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png/350px-2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png/525px-2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png/700px-2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="520"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Benin_Products_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Benin Exports by Product (2014) from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://atlas.cid.harvard.edu/explore/tree_map/export/ben/all/show/2014/">Harvard Atlas of Economic Complexity</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg/220px-Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg/330px-Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg/440px-Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Extensive_Landwirtschaft_im_Norden_Benins_bei_Djougou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Extensive agriculture in the north of Benin, near Djougou.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of Benin is dependent on <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> production, and regional trade. Cotton accounts for 40% of the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> and roughly 80% of official <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> receipts.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Growth in real output has averaged around 5% in the past seven years, but rapid population growth has offset much of this increase.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2018)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> Inflation has subsided over the past several years. Benin uses the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a>, which is pegged to the euro. </p>
      <p>Benin's economy has continued to strengthen over the past years, with real GDP growth estimated at 5.1 and 5.7% in 2008 and 2009, respectively. The main driver of growth is the agricultural sector, with cotton being the country's main export, while services continue to contribute the largest part of GDP largely because of Benin's geographical location, enabling trade, transportation, transit and tourism activities with its neighboring states.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Benin's overall macroeconomic conditions were positive in 2017, with a growth rate of around 5.6 percent. Economic growth was largely driven by Benin's cotton industry and other cash crops, the Port of Cotonou, and telecommunications. Cashew and pineapple production and processing have substantial commercial potential. The country's primary source of revenue is the Port of Cotonou, although the government is seeking to expand its revenue base. In 2017, Benin imported about $2.8 billion in goods such as rice, meat and poultry, alcoholic beverages, fuel plastic materials, specialized mining and excavating machinery, telecommunications equipment, passenger vehicles, and toiletries and cosmetics. Principal exports are ginned cotton, cotton cake and cotton seeds, cashew, shea butter, cooking oil, and lumber.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Benin is lower than world average. In 2016, Benin had 0.9 global hectares <sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-64">[64]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In 2016 Benin used 1.4 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use slightly under double as much biocapacity as Benin contains. As a result, Benin is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG/220px-Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG/330px-Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG/440px-Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gossypium_sp_MS4007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cotton field in northern Benin.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In order to raise growth still further, Benin plans to attract more foreign investment, place more emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Benin" title="Tourism in Benin">tourism</a>, facilitate the development of new food processing systems and agricultural products, and encourage new information and communication technology. Projects to improve the business climate by reforms to the land tenure system, the commercial justice system, and the financial sector were included in Benin's US$307 million <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Account" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Challenge Account">Millennium Challenge Account</a> grant signed in February 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-MCC_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCC-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> and bilateral creditors have eased the external debt situation, with Benin benefiting from a G8 debt reduction announced in July 2005, while pressing for more rapid structural reforms. An insufficient electrical supply continues to adversely affect Benin's economic growth though the government recently has taken steps to increase domestic power production.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although <a href="/wiki/Trade_unions_in_Benin" title="Trade unions in Benin">trade unions in Benin</a> represent up to 75% of the formal workforce, the large informal economy has been noted by the <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a> (ITCU) to contain ongoing problems, including a lack of women's wage equality, the use of <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labor</a>, and the continuing issue of <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Unfree labour">forced labor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Benin is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Cotonou has the country's only seaport and <a href="/wiki/Cadjehoun_Airport" title="Cadjehoun Airport">international airport</a>. A new port is currently under construction between Cotonou and Porto Novo. Benin is connected by two-lane asphalted roads to its neighboring countries (Togo, Burkina Faso, Niger, and Nigeria). Mobile telephone service is available across the country through various <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Network_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile Network Code">operators</a>. ADSL connections are available in some areas. Benin is connected to the Internet by way of satellite connections (since 1998) and a single submarine cable <a href="/wiki/SAT-3/WASC_(cable_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="SAT-3/WASC (cable system)">SAT-3/WASC</a> (since 2001), keeping the price of data extremely high. Relief is expected with the initiation of the <a href="/wiki/ACE_(cable_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="ACE (cable system)">Africa Coast to Europe</a> cable in 2011. </p>
      <p>Despite the GDP growth rate of 4-5% remaining consistent over the past two decades, poverty has been increasing.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> According to the National Institute of Statistics and Economic Analysis in Benin, those living under the poverty line have increased from 36.2% in 2011 to 40.1% in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg/220px-BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg/330px-BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg/440px-BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1338"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BEN_2001-007-S20.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beninese students.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Benin" title="Education in Benin">Education in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate in Benin is among the lowest in the world: in 2015 it was estimated to be 38.4% (49.9% for males and 27.3% for females).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-48">[48]</a></sup> Benin has achieved universal primary education and half of the children (54%) were enrolled in secondary education in 2013, according to the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>. </p>
      <p>Although at one time the education system was not free,<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-71">[71]</a></sup> Benin has abolished school fees and is carrying out the recommendations of its 2007 Educational Forum.<sup id="cite_ref-UnescoBenin_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnescoBenin-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government has devoted more than 4% of GDP to education since 2009. In 2015, public expenditure on education (all levels) amounted to 4.4% of GDP, according to the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>. Within this expenditure, Benin devoted quite a large share to tertiary education: 0.97% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2009 and 2011, the share of young people enrolled at university rose from 10% to 12% of the 18<i>–</i>25 year age cohort, one of the highest ratios in West Africa. Student enrollment in tertiary education more than doubled between 2006 and 2011 from 50,225 to 110,181. These statistics encompass not only bachelor's, master's and Ph.D. programmes but also students enrolled in non-degree post-secondary diplomas.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Benin" title="Science and technology in Benin">Science and technology in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_policy_framework">National policy framework</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: National policy framework">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Higher_Education_and_Scientific_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Higher Education and Scientific Research">Ministry of Higher Education and Scientific Research</a> is responsible for implementing science policy. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Directorate_of_Scientific_and_Technological_Research&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Directorate of Scientific and Technological Research (page does not exist)">National Directorate of Scientific and Technological Research</a> handles planning and coordination, whereas the <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Council_for_Scientific_and_Technical_Research_and_National_Academy_of_Sciences,_Arts,_and_Letters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Council for Scientific and Technical Research and National Academy of Sciences, Arts, and Letters (page does not exist)">National Council for Scientific and Technical Research and National Academy of Sciences, Arts, and Letters</a> each play an advisory role. Financial support comes from Benin's <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Fund_for_Scientific_Research_and_Technological_Innovation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Fund for Scientific Research and Technological Innovation (page does not exist)">National Fund for Scientific Research and Technological Innovation</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Benin_Agency_for_the_Promotion_of_Research_Results_and_Technological_Innovation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Benin Agency for the Promotion of Research Results and Technological Innovation (page does not exist)">The Benin Agency for the Promotion of Research Results and Technological Innovation</a> carries out technology transfer through the development and dissemination of research results.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The regulatory framework has evolved since 2006 till date when the country's first science policy was prepared. This has since been updated and complemented by new texts on science and innovation (the year of adoption is between brackets):<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>a manual for monitoring and evaluating research structures and organizations (2013);</li> 
       <li>a manual on how to select research programmes and projects and apply to the National Fund for Scientific Research and Technological Innovation (2013) for competitive grants;</li> 
       <li>a draft act for funding scientific research and innovation and a draft code of ethics for scientific research and innovation were both submitted to the Supreme Court in 2014;</li> 
       <li>a strategic plan for scientific research and innovation (under development in 2015).</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Equally important are Benin's efforts to integrate science into existing policy documents: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i>Benin Development Strategies 2025</i>: <i>Benin 2025 Alafia</i> (2000);</li> 
       <li>Growt<i>h Strategy for Poverty Reduction 2011–2016</i> (2011);</li> 
       <li>Phase 3 of the <i>Ten-year Development Plan for the Education Sector</i>, covering 2013–2015;</li> 
       <li><i>Development Plan for Higher Education and Scientific Research 2013–2017</i> (2014).</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>In 2015, Benin's priority areas for scientific research were: health, education, construction and building materials, transportation and trade, culture, tourism and handicrafts, cotton/textiles, food, energy and climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The main challenges facing research and development in Benin are:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>the unfavorable organizational framework for research: weak governance, a lack of co-operation between research structures and the absence of an official document on the status of researchers;</li> 
       <li>the inadequate use of human resources and the lack of any motivational policy for researchers; and</li> 
       <li>the mismatch between research and development needs.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_and_financial_investment_in_research">Human and financial investment in research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Human and financial investment in research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2007, Benin counted 1,000 researchers (in headcounts). This corresponds to 115 researchers per million inhabitants. The main research structures in Benin are the Centre for Scientific and Technical Research, National Institute of Agricultural Research, National Institute for Training and Research in Education, Office of Geological and Mining Research and the Centre for Entomological Research.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The University of Abomey-Calavi was selected by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2014 to participate in its Centres of Excellence project, owing to its expertise in applied mathematics. Within this project, the World Bank has loaned $8 million to Benin. The Association of African Universities has also received funds to enable it to co-ordinate knowledge-sharing among the 19 universities in West Africa involved in the project.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are no available data on Benin's level of investment in research and development.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, the government devoted 2.5% of GDP to public health. In December 2014, 150 volunteer health professionals travelled to Guinea, Liberia and Sierra Leone from Benin, Côte d'Ivoire, Ghana, Mali, Niger, and Nigeria, as part of a joint initiative by the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS) and its specialized agency, the West African Health Organisation, to help combat the epidemic. The Ebola epidemic has been a tragic reminder of the chronic underinvestment in West African health systems.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Government of Benin devoted less than 5% of GDP to agricultural development in 2010, even though the members of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> had agreed to commit at least 10% of GDP to this area in the <i>Maputo Declaration</i> of 2003. They reiterated this goal in the <i>Malabo Declaration</i> adopted in Equatorial Guinea in 2014. In the latter declaration, they reaffirmed their 'intention to devote 10% of their national budgets to agricultural development and agreed to targets such as doubling agricultural productivity, halving post-harvest loss and bringing stunting down to 10% across Africa'. However, African leaders meeting in Equatorial Guinea failed to resolve the debate on establishing a common standard of measurement for the 10% target.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_output">Research output</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research output">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Benin has the third-highest publication intensity for scientific journals in West Africa, according to Thomson Reuters' Web of Science, Science Citation Index Expanded. There were 25.5 scientific articles per million inhabitants cataloged in this database in 2014. This compares with 65.0 for the Gambia, 49.6 for Cape Verde, 23.2 for Senegal and 21.9 for Ghana. The volume of publications in this database tripled in Benin between 2005 and 2014 from 86 to 270. Between 2008 and 2014, Benin's main scientific collaborators were based in France (529 articles), United States (261), United Kingdom (254), Belgium (198) and Germany (156).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Benin" title="Transport in Benin">Transport in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Benin" title="Transport in Benin">Transport in Benin</a> includes road, rail, water and air transportation. Benin possesses a total of 6,787&nbsp;km of <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highway</a>, of which 1,357&nbsp;km are paved. Of the paved highways in the country, there are 10 <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">expressways</a>. This leaves 5,430&nbsp;km of unpaved road. The <a href="/wiki/Trans%E2%80%93West_African_Coastal_Highway" title="Trans–West African Coastal Highway">Trans-West African Coastal Highway</a> crosses Benin, connecting it to <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to the west. When construction in <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> is finished, the highway will continue west to seven other <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS) nations. A paved highway also connects Benin northwards to <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, and through that country to <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to the north-west. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Benin" title="Rail transport in Benin">Rail transport in Benin</a> consists of 578&nbsp;km (359&nbsp;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Single_track_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Single track (rail)">single track</a>, <span class="nowrap">1,000&nbsp;mm</span> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="nowrap">3&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac" role="math">3<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">3</span>⁄<span class="den">8</span></span>&nbsp;in</span>) <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Metre_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Metre gauge">metre gauge</a></span> railway. Benin does not, at this time, share railway links with adjacent countries, but construction work has commenced on international lines connecting Benin with Niger and Nigeria, with outline plans announced for further connections to Togo and Burkina Faso. Benin will be a participant in the <a href="/wiki/AfricaRail" title="AfricaRail">AfricaRail</a> project. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cadjehoun_Airport" title="Cadjehoun Airport">Cadjehoun Airport</a>, located at Cotonou, has direct international jet service to <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, Niamey, <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">Lagos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9" title="Lomé">Lomé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, as well as other cities in Africa. Direct services also link Cotonou to Paris, Brussels, and Istanbul. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Benin" title="Health in Benin">Health in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Benin" title="HIV/AIDS in Benin">HIV/AIDS in Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> rate in Benin was estimated in 2013 at 1.13% of adults aged 15–49 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA3_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA3-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is a problem in Benin, being a leading cause of morbidity and mortality among children younger than five years.<sup id="cite_ref-Malaria_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malaria-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1980s, less than 30% of the country's population had access to primary health care services. Benin had one of the highest death rates for children under the age of five in the world. Its <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> stood at 203 deaths for every <span style="white-space:nowrap">1<span style="margin-left:0.25em">000</span></span> live births. Only one in three mothers had access to child health care services. The <a href="/wiki/Bamako_Initiative" title="Bamako Initiative">Bamako Initiative</a> changed that dramatically by introducing community-based healthcare reform, resulting in more efficient and equitable provision of services.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Benin had the 26th highest rate of <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA2-78">[78]</a></sup> According to a 2013 UNICEF report, 13% of women had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-79">[79]</a></sup> A comprehensive approach strategy was extended to all areas of healthcare, with subsequent improvement in the health care indicators and improvement in health care efficiency and cost.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> has completed three surveys in Benin since 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Benin_Surveys_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benin_Surveys-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg/220px-Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg/330px-Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg/440px-Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palais_Des_Congres_De_Cotonou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Palais Des Congres in <a href="/wiki/Cotonou" title="Cotonou">Cotonou</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Benin_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Benin literature">Benin literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Benin" title="Music of Benin">Music of Benin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Benin" title="Cinema of Benin">Cinema of Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg/220px-Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg/330px-Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg/440px-Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Who%27s_coming_%3F.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional music group.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Beninese literature had a strong oral tradition long before French became the dominant language.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Couchoro" title="Félix Couchoro">Félix Couchoro</a> wrote the first Beninese novel, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=L%27Esclave_(Beninese_novel)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="L'Esclave (Beninese novel) (page does not exist)">L'Esclave</a></i> (The Slave), in 1929. </p>
      <p>Post-independence, the country was home to a vibrant and innovative music scene, where native folk music combined with <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghanaian</a> <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a>, French <a href="/wiki/Cabaret" title="Cabaret">cabaret</a>, American <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Music of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> <a href="/wiki/African_Rumba" class="mw-redirect" title="African Rumba">rumba</a>. </p>
      <p>Singer <a href="/wiki/Ang%C3%A9lique_Kidjo" title="Angélique Kidjo">Angélique Kidjo</a> and actor <a href="/wiki/Djimon_Hounsou" title="Djimon Hounsou">Djimon Hounsou</a> were born in Cotonou, Benin. Composer <a href="/wiki/Wally_Badarou" title="Wally Badarou">Wally Badarou</a> and singer <a href="/wiki/Gnonnas_Pedro" title="Gnonnas Pedro">Gnonnas Pedro</a> are also of Beninese descent. </p>
      <p>Biennale Benin, continuing the projects of several organizations and artists, started in the country in 2010 as a collaborative event called "Regard Benin". In 2012, the project became a Biennial coordinated by the Consortium, a federation of local associations. The international exhibition and artistic program of the 2012 Biennale Benin are curated by Abdellah Karroum and the Curatorial Delegation. </p>
      <p>A number of Beninese artists have received major international recognition, such as <a href="/wiki/Georges_Ad%C3%A9agbo" title="Georges Adéagbo">Georges Adéagbo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meschac_Gaba" title="Meschac Gaba">Meschac Gaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romuald_Hazoum%C3%A8" title="Romuald Hazoumè">Romuald Hazoumè</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominique_Zinkp%C3%A8&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dominique Zinkpè (page does not exist)">Dominique Zinkpè</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominique_Zinkp%C3%A8" class="extiw" title="fr:Dominique Zinkpè">fr</a>]</span> and <a href="/wiki/Emo_de_Medeiros" title="Emo de Medeiros">Emo de Medeiros</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customary_names">Customary names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Customary names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Many Beninese in the south of the country have <a href="/wiki/Akan_name" class="mw-redirect" title="Akan name">Akan-based names</a> indicating the day of the week on which they were born. This is due to influence of the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan people</a> like the <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Benin" title="Languages of Benin">Languages of Benin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Local languages are used as the languages of instruction in elementary schools, with French only introduced after several years. In wealthier cities, however, French is usually taught at an earlier age. At the secondary school level, local language is generally forbidden and French is the sole language of instruction. Beninese languages are generally transcribed with a separate letter for each speech sound (<a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phoneme</a>), rather than using <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a> as in French or <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">digraphs</a> as in English. This includes Beninese <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">Yoruba</a>, which in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> is written with both diacritics and digraphs. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Mid_vowel" title="Mid vowel">mid vowels</a> written <i>é, è, ô, o</i> in French are written <i><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">e, ɛ, o, ɔ</span></i> in Beninese languages, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">consonants</a> are written <i>ng</i> and <i>sh</i> or <i>ch</i> in English are written <i>ŋ</i> and <i>c.</i> However, digraphs are used for <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">nasal vowels</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Labial-velar_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Labial-velar consonant">labial-velar consonants</a> <i>kp</i> and <i>gb,</i> as in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Fon_language" title="Fon language">Fon language</a> <i>Fon gbe</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/fõ ɡ͡be/</span>, and diacritics are used as <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tone marks</a>. In French-language publications, a mixture of French and Beninese orthographies may be seen. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bahia_acaraje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bahia_acaraje.jpg/220px-Bahia_acaraje.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bahia_acaraje.jpg/330px-Bahia_acaraje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bahia_acaraje.jpg/440px-Bahia_acaraje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1291" data-file-height="968"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bahia_acaraje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Acaraj%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Acarajé">Acarajé</a> is peeled <a href="/wiki/Black-eyed_pea" title="Black-eyed pea">black-eyed peas</a> formed into a ball and then deep-fried.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Benin_cuisine" title="Benin cuisine">Benin cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Beninese cuisine is known in Africa for its exotic ingredients and flavorful dishes. Beninese cuisine involves fresh meals served with a variety of key sauces. In southern Benin cuisine, the most common ingredient is <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, often used to prepare <a href="/wiki/Dough" title="Dough">dough</a> which is mainly served with <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanut</a>- or <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Sauce" title="Sauce">sauces</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">Fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a> are the most common meats used in southern Beninese cuisine, but <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aethomys" title="Aethomys">bush rat</a> are also consumed. The main staple in northern Benin is <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, often served with sauces mentioned above. The population in the northern provinces use beef and <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> meat which is fried in palm or peanut oil or cooked in sauces. <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">Cheese</a> is used in some dishes. <a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">Couscous</a>, rice, and <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a> are commonly eaten, along with fruits such as <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a>, oranges, avocados, bananas, kiwi fruit, and pineapples. </p>
      <p>Meat is usually quite expensive, and meals are generally light on meat and generous on <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_fat" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetable fat">vegetable fat</a>. Frying in palm or peanut oil is the most common meat preparation, and <a href="/wiki/Smoked_fish" title="Smoked fish">smoked fish</a> is commonly prepared in Benin. Grinders are used to prepare <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">corn flour</a>, which is made into a dough and served with sauces. "Chicken on the spit" is a traditional recipe in which chicken is roasted over a fire on wooden sticks. <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">Palm</a> roots are sometimes soaked in a jar with salt water and sliced garlic to tenderize them, then used in dishes. Many people have outdoor mud stoves for cooking. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is generally considered the most popular sport in Benin. In the past decade, <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> has been introduced to the country.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
